I was one of the avid customer coming every weekend. Last 3 not so good. The meet is not fully cooked and hard. For the past 2 times my order was wrong as they pack it to go. For 2 tortillas with the same amount of meat as 1 taco.

I can tell you they lost a regular, I'm sure they don't care as they are on a very popular street i found another place is called Red teddy's tacos. Its abit of a drive but its worth it  . Exremely unprofessional company. Took many months to close a refinance. Information on documents was constantly wrong, the needed changes had to be requested many times and in some cases were still wrong.

It is impossible to get a hold of them. They don't return calls, they don't return emails. They are rude and short with you when you do finally get a hold of them.

When the mobile notary arrived to sign the final documents they were largely incorrect and he had to be sent home. The second time he came back half of the documents were blank and he had no idea what was supposed to go where.

They did the title paperwork wrong.

Overall an extremely amateur performance of a serious and complicated transaction. Avoid this company at all costs!</text>

<review>High quality ingredients. Honest, homemade cuisine. Very friendly chef and staff.</review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPbAdN6p6g34tm8_UNSgF2f2AN7aBFDC1iHf5Ru=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics><Resp>None</Resp><gmapID>0x808417339b60f215:0x9c36dc8e12aaac8d</gmapID></record></dataset><record>
<UserId.>108896539890181663262< /UserId.>< Name>
John Gainey< /Name>
<Date>1550177656543</Date><rate>5</rate><Text>Guiso! (pronounced [EE-soh]) From the time that we walked through the door until the moment we left, we felt like part of Chef Carlos's extended family.

The Good: Lets start, for once, with the staff.  Valeria, our server, was such a friendly and fun person that we felt more like we were having a meal with friends rather than at a restaurant.  Don't get me wrong, she was professional and efficient, but made us feel completely at home.  She explained the menu and the concept behind the restaurant and told us a few of her favorite menu items.  We also met Chef Carlos later in the meal. We had been watching him move through the open kitchen all evening, and it was nice of him to take the time to come to the table and say hello.
Now on to the food.  The first appetizer we had was the Brucelas con Chorizo.  There were so many interesting flavors popping up through this dish between the house made chorizo and the crema and the jerk flavored butter, that every bite brought a new, welcome layer to dish.  We shared it between 3 people, and while it started out with everyone being willing to share, it rapidly turned into a mini brawl to see who would get the last spoonful of brussel sprouts. Now when is the last time you could say that?!   Next there was the Media Noche Sliders described as mojo marinated pork shoulder, smoked ham, homemade sweet pickles, mustard, and Swiss cheese. These were good, but not quite the wow factor of the brussel sprouts.  We found that for our tastes, if we pulled one of the two pickles off each slider it dropped the acidity level to a more pleasant counter note.  The pulled pork was a little on the salty side, but the homemade rolls were soft and delightful. Last appy was the Guiso Vegetariano.  This is a don't miss menu item in my opinion.  Valeria described it as vegetables in a tomato based stew, but I don't think that really describes it well enough.  The vegetables in the guiso vary with seasonal availability, and ours contained potatoes, sugar snap peas, baby squash, and a few others that all tasted so fresh and well prepared that I thought they might have come out of someone's garden.  But the real star of this dish is the guiso/stew base.  This isn't just another tired ragout.  There layered flavors in this stew that that go way past tomato sauce and add delicate cumin and chile spices that dance around the vegetables celebrating their freshness.  DO give this a try.  Evidently he uses the same guiso base for his shrimp appetizer, but since I don't do seafood (unfortunately) we did not get that one.
The stew base was so good that we ordered the house made rolls JUST TO SOAK UP ALL THE GUISO LIQUID IN THE BOWL!  The entrees were also quite satisfying.  I ate the After Church Burger which was small but very tasty accompanied by tarragon roasted potatoes with a really tasty yogurt chile sauce for dipping.   I'd order it again just to get that sauce.  My table mates ordered the Paella Caribena which was more soupy than the dryer rice-heavy versions I have seen elsewhere.  I mentioned earlier that I don't eat seafood.  I wish I could because most of it looks very appealing, but the smell usually causes my stomach to turn. The paella arrived with chicken, linguisa, prawns and clams looking more like a cioppino than a paella, but it smelled absolutely wonderful.  Even my sensitive nose couldn't detect any seafood smells whatsoever.  By my table mate's accounts, it tasted as incredible as it smelled.

The Bad:  Nothing.

The Mediocre:  There were no pupusas that night because the chef's mother, who makes them, had just arrived back from traveling from El Salvador.  How dare she take personal time to recover from jet lag instead on making me a pupusa?! Such Nerve.

Overall:  This is a very nice, comfortable, homey place to enjoy a meal that uses Salvadorian spices and influence to elevate their food.  I can't tell you the last time I enjoyed a meal this much.  So run, don't walk to see chef Carlos and his family at Guiso!!!</Text>< Pics>

<Text>After a disappointing overpriced experience at Valette around the corner, Chef Carlos was a breath of fresh air. Honest but well crafted dishes that exceeded expectations. The Camerones Borracho were intriguingly Indian in style with a splash of cummin but still had a foot in the Americas. The pupusas were as authentic as you can get but delightfully presented. The Chicken en Chili Verde was so nicely balanced in flavor - a subtle heat, sublimely juicy and tender chicken breast, accompanied with garden vegetables. Lastly, the paella was unlike any you will have encountered before. Rich, but not heavy. Each element was clearly standing apart yet contributing to the whole. Many paellas end up being a messy fusion of flavors but this one was at once both rich and distinct. Save yourself some money and dine at Guiso before you book at the other Healdsburg regulars.<//Text>< user_id>

< Review>
I really hate to leave a review for this place. Why? Because I may have to fight you for a table. This place is amazing. The food is action packed with a delicate balance of strong flavours that harmonious work to tantalise your taste buds.

The chef is very patient with my adversion to spicy heat and is still able to deliver food that brings tears of joy to my eyes.

Our server (whom I am ashamed to admit's name escapes me) is delightful, knowledgeable and has great presence! He really engages and remembers guests and conversations.

The Fish and the Veggie tacos are my personal favourite!! Though you cannot go wrong with any of them!

See you Tuesday, save me a table!!

We have been visiting Taco night, weekly, for almost two months now for work and Tuesday is not a Tuesday without Guiso's Tacos!</Review>

<Time>1498073706566<//Time><Rate>5< /Rate><text>My wife and I walked around Healdsburg looking at the menus for most of the restaurants nearby. The prices were high and the items on the menu did not make much sense.

Then by accident, we found Guiso tucked away next to the Raven theater.
We were greated right away and given a table. The atmosphere is warm and inviting. Almost like a family dining table with the chef cooking in view of the guests.

The menu has tapas style dishes and a few entrees.  The food was amazing. I definitely recommend the Cubanitas sliders.

By the end of the meal my wife and I were the only ones left in the restaurant on a Sunday evening. Rather than trying to rush us out so they could close the chef took the time to talk to us about the restaurant and the food for awhile before we left.

Already having low confidence issues, he had started to growl at humans and other dogs in fear at 14 weeks. He was a bit older than the junior group but inexperienced so they put together a custom schedule to get him into juniors and to move up into intermediate classes. When we initially brought him into his first class he was scared and growled and snapped at other puppies.
